The Mu'tazila Claim: Attributes Are Not Eternal
Baqillani presents the Mu'tazila view that attributes are merely created descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila doctrine that divine attributes are merely descriptions created by humans and that God had no attributes in preexistence.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila reduce attributes to human speech, denying God's eternal qualities.

Imam al-Baqillani begins by presenting the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya claim about divine attributes. They argue that an attribute is nothing more than a description spoken by a person, so God could not have had attributes before creation. This lesson examines their reasoning and its radical implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about their claim
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall argument. Then read the translation.
Notice how they define attribute (ṣifa) as description (waṣf).
2
Identify their key claim
The Mu'tazila equate attribute with description, which is human speech. This is a crucial reduction.
3
Understand their inference
Since God could not describe Himself before creating speech (due to their belief in created speech), they conclude God had no attributes in preexistence.
4
Grasp their radical conclusion
They claim that creation gives God names and attributes because they produce the speech that describes Him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد زعمت المعتزلة القدرية وكل من اغتر بشبههم من أهل الأهواء المضلّة، أن الصفة ليست بمعنى أكثر من الوصف الذي هو قول القائل وإخبار المخبر عمن أخبر عنه بأنه عالم قادر وتفحموا القول بأن الله تعالى كان في أزله بلا صفة ولا اسم من أسمائه وصفاته العليا. قالوا : لأنه لا يجوز أن يكون في القدم واصفاً لنفسه لاعتقادهم خلق كلامه ولا يجوز أن يكون في القدم واصف له مخبر عما هو عليه. فوجب أنه لا صفة الله سبحانه قبل أن يخلق خلقه، وأن الخلق هم الذين يجعلون الله الأسماء والصفات لأنهم هم الخالقون لأقوالهم التي صفات الله سبحانه وأسماؤه. لأنهم أيضاً يزعمون أن الاسم هو التسمية وهو قول المسمّى الله تعالى، وأن الله سبحانه كان قبل خلق كل من كلّمه وأمره ونهاه، بلا اسم ولا صفة . فلما أوجد العباد خلقوا له الأسماء والصفات تعالى عن ذلك. وهذا القول خروج عما عليه كافة الأمة قبل خلق المعتزلة ووجودهم. مع أنهم أيضاً عند تضييق الكلام عليهم وتحصيله يُرهبون أتباعهم ومخالفيهم من الإخبار عن حقيقة قولهم هذا، ولا يطلقون أن الله تعالى كان قبل خلق عباده بلا اسم ولا صفة، وأن العباد هم الذين خلقوا الله تعالى الأسماء والصفات. ويخافون تخطف الناس لهم وبسط أيديهم عليهم، علماً منهم بأنه مخالفة للإجماع ومما ينفر عنه الخواص والعوام.
And the Qadariyya Mu'tazila and everyone who is deceived by their fallacies from the people of misguidance have claimed that the attribute (ṣifa) is not a meaning (maʿnā) more than the description (waṣf) which is the speech of the speaker and the report of the reporter about whom he reported that he is knowing, able. And they made it difficult to say that Allah, exalted, was in His preexistence without attribute and without any name from His names and His lofty attributes. They said: Because it is not permissible for Him to be in preexistence describing Himself due to their belief in the creation of His speech, and it is not permissible for Him in preexistence to be a describer and reporter of what He is. So it became necessary that Allah, glorified, has no attribute before He created His creation, and that the creation are the ones who give Allah the names and attributes because they are the creators of their statements which are the attributes of Allah and His names. And because they also claim that the name (ism) is the naming (tasmiya) and it is the statement of the one named Allah, and that Allah, glorified, was before creating everyone He spoke to, commanded, and forbade, without name and without attribute. So when the servants brought into existence, they created for Him the names and attributes—exalted is He above that. And this statement is a departure from what the entire community (umma) was upon before the creation of the Mu'tazila and their existence. And along with that, when speech is tightened upon them and investigated, they frighten their followers and opponents from reporting the reality of this statement of theirs, and they do not state openly that Allah was before the creation of His servants without name and attribute, and that the servants created for Allah the names and attributes. And they fear that people will seize them and extend their hands upon them, knowing from themselves that it is opposition to consensus (ijmāʿ) and something that repels the elite and the commoners.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya position on divine attributes. Baqillani begins by stating their claim: that attribute (ṣifa) is nothing more than description (waṣf), which is the speech of the speaker. They deny that God had any attributes or names in preexistence. Their reasoning: since they believe God's speech is created, He could not have been describing Himself in preexistence. Therefore, they conclude that God had no attributes until He created, and that the creation actually give God names and attributes because they produce the speech that describes Him. Baqillani then points out that this contradicts the consensus of the entire Muslim community before the Mu'tazila appeared. Moreover, he notes that the Mu'tazila themselves are hesitant to openly state this position; they frighten their followers and opponents from revealing the true implications of their doctrine. They fear public backlash and physical harm, knowing that their view violates consensus and repels both scholars and commoners. Baqillani highlights the hypocrisy of the Mu'tazila who hide the full ramifications of their theology.

Key Terms
صفة (ṣifa)
وصف (waṣf)
معنى (maʿnā)
قديم (qadīm)
خلق الكلام (khalq al-kalām)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila, what is an attribute (ṣifa)?
A) A real eternal quality of God
B) A description spoken by a person
C) A divine name
D) A mode of God's essence

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila deny eternal attributes by reducing them to human descriptions, making creation the source of God's attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself describing God in a way that made Him fit your own expectations or limited understanding? How does the Mu'tazila error warn you against reducing God to your own words?
?
If you truly believed that God's attributes were merely human inventions, how would that change your worship and trust in Him? Would you still pray to a God whose qualities you yourself created?
?
When you recite the names of Allah, do you treat them as eternal realities revealing who He is, or as comfortable labels? Pause and consider: if His attributes were not real and eternal, what would that mean for your hope in His mercy and power?

Baqillani's Refutation: Consensus and Hypocrisy
Baqillani refutes the Mu'tazila by consensus and their own hypocrisy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's refutation of the Mu'tazila claim, based on consensus of the umma and the Mu'tazila's own reluctance to openly state their position.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila doctrine contradicts consensus, and they hide its full implications.

After presenting the Mu'tazila claim, Imam al-Baqillani refutes it by pointing out two telling facts. First, their view contradicts the consensus of the entire Muslim community before their time. Second, they themselves are afraid to openly state their doctrine, revealing its falsehood.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully, focusing on the refutation arguments.
2
Identify the first refutation
Baqillani invokes consensus (ijmāʿ): the Mu'tazila position is a departure from what the entire umma held before them.
3
Identify the second refutation
He points out that the Mu'tazila themselves are reluctant to openly state their radical conclusions, fearing public backlash.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consensus is a powerful proof in Sunni theology, and the Mu'tazila's concealment shows the weakness of their position.

Source Text

Consensus as Proof for Real Attributes
Baqillani uses Islamic consensus on divine attributes to argue speech is not an attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consensus of the Muslim community on divine attributes refutes the claim that attributes are merely descriptions and supports the view that speech is a distinct attribute.

Core Idea
Consensus confirms that God's attributes are real, not just labels.

Imam al-Baqillani presents a second proof for the reality of divine attributes by appealing to the consensus of the ummah. The entire community agrees that attributes like justice and beneficence are truly attributes of God, not mere descriptions. This agreement directly counters the opponent's claim that the attribute is nothing more than a description.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Notice the key terms and the structure of the argument.
The passage is concise but packs a logical punch.
2
Identify the core consensus claim
Look for the phrase 'إجماع الأمة قاطبة' and note what the ummah agrees upon. Why is this important for theology?
3
Understand how consensus refutes the opponent's view
The opponent says an attribute is only a description. The consensus shows that justice and beneficence are real attributes, not just descriptions. How does that undermine the opponent?
Think about the difference between God being just (attribute) and us describing Him as just (description).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يدل على ذلك أيضاً إجماع الأمة قاطبة على أن العدل والإحسان من صفات الله تعالى وأن من قال : إن العدل والإحسان صفات الله فقد فارق ما عليه المسلمون. وهذا الإجماع أيضاً يبطل قولهم إن الصفة ليست بمعنى أكثر من الوصف، لأن العدل والإحسان الذي يفعله الله تعالى ليس بقول ولا وصف لواصف.
And among the evidence for that also is the consensus of the entire community that justice and beneficence are among the attributes of God Most High and that whoever says that justice and beneficence are attributes of God has departed from what the Muslims are upon. And this consensus also invalidates their saying that the attribute is nothing more than the description, because the justice and beneficence that God Most High does is not a speech nor a description of a describer.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This second proof appeals to Islamic consensus on divine attributes. The ummah agrees that attributes like justice (al-ʿadl) and beneficence (al-iḥsān) are truly attributes of God, not mere descriptions. If someone says these are God's attributes, he is correct. This consensus refutes the claim that an attribute is nothing more than a description (al-waṣf). The justice God does is not a speech act or a human description; it is a real attribute. Hence, speech cannot be the same as attribute.

Key Terms
إجماع الأمة
العدل
الإحسان
صفات الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that calling God 'just' is merely a human description; the consensus shows that justice is a real attribute of God, not just a label.
Correction: The consensus of the ummah is that justice and beneficence are real attributes of God, not mere descriptions.

Checkpoint
According to the consensus cited by Baqillani, what are justice and beneficence?
A) Only human descriptions of God
B) Real attributes of God
C) Speeches about God
D) Metaphors for God's actions

Key Takeaway
The consensus of the ummah on divine attributes proves that attributes are real and distinct from their descriptions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe that God is just and beneficent. But do you truly treat these as real, objective attributes of God that shape how you live—or are they just nice-sounding labels you use without letting them disturb your comfort? Pause and ask yourself: when you act unjustly or fail in kindness, do you remember that you are violating a real attribute of Allah?
?
The consensus of the ummah binds you to affirm that justice and beneficence are real attributes of God. Are there any points in your life where you hesitate to submit to this consensus, perhaps preferring your own reasoning over the unified testimony of the believers? Will you today consciously align your heart with the community of Muslims on this matter?
?
Baqillani says that denying justice as an attribute of God is to depart from what the Muslims are upon. Have you ever casually entertained ideas about God's attributes that contradict this consensus? Right now, commit to purifying your theology of any doubt or innovation regarding God's real attributes.
